---
title: "Installing Ubuntu 14.04 on Inspiron 14 7000 for Dual Boot"
date: 2014-09-03
forum: New to Ubuntu
---

### Post by Ben_C on 2014-09-03
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]I'm as new as you can get with Linux and I'm trying to install Ubuntu on my machine so I can dual boot between Windows 8.1 which came pre-installed and Ubuntu.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]I've been on a lot of forums already; I have a USB in with the install and it goes well until it gets to the Installation Type page which is blank.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]I know a few websites said to turn off Intel Smart Response Technology, in my BIOS I have the option to change SATA to AHCI. Is that what I should do? Can I change it back after the install?[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]One site also had me turn off secureboot, can I turn this back on after the install too?[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]I also read there might be some trouble because there is some sort of SSD on this computer along side the HDD, I don't understand how to fix that though.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]This is the link for my laptop with the specs [http://www.dell.com/us/p/inspiron-14-7437/pd](http://www.dell.com/us/p/inspiron-14-7437/pd)[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]I'll also attach a picture of my disk management, I feel like there are too many ones here, and the U: drive I made for Ubuntu, I don't know if I did it correctly though.[/FONT][/COLOR]
[COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]Thanks in advanced for your help everyone[ATTACH=CONFIG]256095[/ATTACH][/FONT][/COLOR]

---

### Post by yancek on 2014-09-03
My understanding is that a pre-installed windows 8 will usually be installed in UEFI mode with GPT partitioning.  You will then need to install UBuntu in EFI mode and there should be an option for that when you boot it or start the install.  Can't be any more detailed as I don't use it.  You should not need to disable Secure Boot to install.  Make sure you shut down windows 8 and reboot the Ubuntu installation medium.  I understand the default for windows 8 is a hibernation mode which can cause problems.  Don't know if this is relevant in your situation.

I don't see how having an SSD attached would cause problems other than user confusion and installing to the wrong drive.  Even that should be easily avoided as you should be able to see the drive size.

> [COLOR=#000000][FONT=Arial]the U: drive I made for Ubuntu, I don't know if I did it correctly though.[/FONT][/COLOR]


No you didn't.  It is formatted ntfs which will not work.  You can't format a Linux filesystem from windows and a default windows can't even read Linux.  You can format during the install.  The number of partitions should not be a problem with GPT.

Boot the Ubuntu medium and select to Try Ubuntu rather than install.  Open a terminal window by simultaneously holding down the Ctrl+Alt+t keys.  When it opens type:  sudo gparted.  This will open a new window which should show your partitions.  You can post the image here.

---

### Post by fantab on 2014-09-04
What worked? Have you installed Ubuntu?

'Trying Ubuntu' post the output of the following command from 'Terminal':
```
sudo parted -l
```

Some OEM's set up SSD as a 'cacheing' device... to speed up Windows. And they set it up with some sort of RAID.... Ubuntu won't install.
If you have an intel board then look in the UEFI for *Intel Smart Response*... you have to disable that.
Windows 8 has 'Fast Startup' feature, which keeps Windows in 'hibernation'... you need to disable that too.
Read [**Here**]("https://help.ubuntu.com/community/UEFI") before you proceed with setting up dual boot with Win and Ubu.

### Post by fantab on 2014-09-04
You can use a blank USB drive as 'cacheing' device: [http://www.thewindowsclub.com/enable-disable-disk-write-caching-windows-7-8](http://www.thewindowsclub.com/enable-disable-disk-write-caching-windows-7-8)

### Post by Ben_C on 2014-09-04

---

### Post by fantab on 2014-09-05
Offcourse you can, but Ubuntu/linux os will not install because Windows uses some kind of proprietory (closed-source) [RAID]("https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/RAID")... which Ubuntu does NOT understand. 

Ubuntu can insall on RAID: [https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Raid](https://wiki.ubuntu.com/Raid) but not with 'special' Raid.
Some users have this setup disabled during ubuntu install and re-enable it after Ubuntu is installed. However, this does not work with all OEMs.

Windows is inherently slow when compared to GNU/Linux Operating Systems... So Windows uses such tweaks like 'FAST STartup', 'Fast boot' and Disk cacheing to speed up things. IMO Windows speed is not improved by much...

### Post by Ben_C on 2014-09-05
I fixed it, you cannot use Intel Rapid Storage with any partitions on the SSD disk so I deleted them and reinstalled Ubuntu and all is right with the world

Thanks everyone who helped me out
